**Result:**

/**  
 * Plugin Builder - Build Status API  
 *  
 * GET /api/plugin-builder/builds/:id - Check build status  
 */  

import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'  
import { getBuildStatus } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  

export async function GET(  
  _request: NextRequest,  
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
) {  
  const { id } = await params  

  const result = await getBuildStatus(id)  

  if (result.error) {  
    return NextResponse.json(  
      { error: result.error },  
      { status: result.status }  
    )  
  }  
  return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
}  

</details>

  setScanResult(null)  
  setError(null)  
}, [url, ref])

Key fixes (in the act4_start_and_register function):  
1. The `portable_sed` replacement for `DEFAULT_AGENT` uses `s|DEFAULT_AGENT=.*|DEFAULT_AGENT=mailman|` — add an anchor `^` to make it `s|^DEFAULT_AGENT=.*|DEFAULT_AGENT=mailman|` to avoid matching lines that contain DEFAULT_AGENT= as part of a larger string.  
2. The `gw_list` variable is built with `\n` literal strings, but when passed to `portable_sed` for replacement, BSD sed (macOS) treats `\n` as literal characters instead of newlines. Fix: after building gw_list, convert the literal `\n` sequences to actual newlines using: on macOS `gw_list=$(printf '%b' "$gw_list")` or by using a printf-based approach that works cross-platform.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:19:52]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a clear picture of all the issues. Let me analyze each one carefully before making changes.  

**Bug 1 (line 1066):** `portable_sed 's|DEFAULT_AGENT=.*|DEFAULT_AGENT=mailman|' .env` — missing `^` anchor. This is in `act3_clone_and_build`.  

**Bug 2 (line 1225-1230):** `gw_list` is built with literal `\n` sequences (e.g. `"${gw_list}\n- ${gw_display}"`), then passed directly to `portable_sed`. On macOS (BSD sed), `\n` in the replacement string is treated as a literal backslash-n, not a newline. The fix is to convert `\n` sequences to actual newlines using `printf '%b'` after building the list. This is in `act4_start_and_register`.  

**Bug 3 (line 1061):** `portable_sed 's|AIMAESTRO_API=.*|AIMAESTRO_API=http://127.0.0.1:${PORT}|' .env` — also in `act3_clone_and_build`. The `${PORT}` variable inside single quotes won't expand, so the literal string `${PORT}` would be written to the file. This needs double quotes. This is an additional bug I can see clearly in the code.

**New:**

            for gw_item in "${GW_ITEMS[@]}"; do
                local gw_display=""
                case "$gw_item" in
                    slack)    gw_display="Slack" ;;
                    discord)  gw_display="Discord" ;;
                    email)    gw_display="Email" ;;

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:20:21]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

All three fixes are correctly applied. Now let me also check whether the `portable_sed` with actual newlines in the replacement string will work correctly. When `gw_list` contains real newlines and is passed inside a double-quoted string to `sed`, the multiline replacement can cause issues with BSD/GNU sed. Let me think through this carefully.  

When `gw_list` contains actual newlines (e.g., `"- Slack\n- Discord"` after `printf '%b'`), and it's interpolated into `portable_sed "s|{{ACTIVE_GATEWAYS_LIST}}|${gw_list}|g"`, the shell expands it to a multi-line argument. BSD sed on macOS handles multi-line replacement strings properly when the newlines come from shell expansion (not from literal `\n` in the sed script). GNU sed also handles this correctly. So the fix is correct.  

Now write the fix report:  

</div>

Key fixes:  
1. Poll failure error is hidden: when polling fails after 5 attempts, `result` is still set (with status: 'building'), so `{error && !result && ...}` hides the error. Fix: add `setResult(null)` before `setError(...)` in both the `>= 5` failure code paths inside the polling interval.  
2. Silent failure in handlePush when `!result?.manifest`: instead of silent `return`, set `setPushResult({ ok: false, message: 'Build manifest not available' })` before returning.  
3. Improve GitHub URL regex from loose `/^https:\/\/github\.com\/.+\/.+/` to `/^https:\/\/github\.com\/[^\/]+\/[^\/]+(\.git)?\/?$/i`.

      return NextResponse.json(

**New:**  
```
    if (!body.url || typeof body.url !== 'string') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Repository URL is required' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    // Validate ref type: if provided it must be a string, not a number/object/etc.
    if (body.ref != null && typeof body.ref !== 'string') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Repository ref must be a string' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    const result = await scanRepo(body.url, body.ref || 'main')

    // Guard against null/undefined or error result from scanRepo
    if (!result || result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result?.error ?? 'Scan failed' },
        { status: result?.status ?? 500 }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data)
  } catch (error) {
    // JSON parse errors from request.json() are client mistakes → 400
    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Invalid request body' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }
    // Any other thrown error is an unexpected server-side failure → 500
    console.error('Error scanning repo:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Internal server error' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:19:30]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the exact code. The bug is on line 214: `skill.id.split(':')[2]` retrieves the third segment (index 2), which is `undefined` if the id has fewer than 3 colon-separated parts (e.g., `plugin-name:skill-name`). The fix is to always get the last segment.  

Now let me also check the `PluginSkillSelection` type to verify the `skill.plugin` and `skill.marketplace` fields for the subtitle bug assessment.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:19:39]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The type definition confirms that for `marketplace` skills, `id`, `marketplace`, and `plugin` are all required (non-optional) fields. So the subtitle issue is NOT a real bug — those fields are always present by the type contract.  

The only real bug is in `getSkillDisplayName` at line 214: `skill.id.split(':')[2]` uses index 2 (third segment), which is `undefined` if the id has fewer than 3 colon-separated parts. The fix is to use `parts[parts.length - 1]` to always get the last segment.  

Now I'll apply the fix.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:19:40]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `PluginComposer.tsx`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-b64901/components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx`  

**Old:**  
```
    case 'marketplace':
      return skill.id.split(':')[2] || skill.id
```

**New:**  
```
    case 'marketplace': {
      // Always get the last colon-separated segment, regardless of how many segments exist
      const parts = skill.id.split(':')
      return parts[parts.length - 1] || skill.id
    }
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-b64901/components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx has been updated successfully.  

</details>

Work in that directory. Fix the highest-severity bugs found in the review report.  

Focus on these specific fixes:  
1. HIGH: `activeOps++` is incremented BEFORE the try block in buildPlugin, scanRepo, and pushToGitHub. If an error occurs before the try block (in evictStaleBuildResults or other pre-try code), activeOps is never decremented. Move `activeOps++` to be the FIRST statement INSIDE the try block in all three functions.  
2. HIGH: In `buildPlugin`, `activeOps` is decremented in the `finally` block but `runBuild` is async-fire-and-forget. The finally runs immediately after launching runBuild, not when it completes. Move the `activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)` decrement into the `runBuild(...).catch(...).finally(...)` chain, and handle the catch-block decrement separately.  
3. HIGH: `SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE` regex `/^[a-zA-Z0-9_-]+$/` is missing the dot character. Paths like `my.skill` or `index.ts` are incorrectly rejected. Fix: add `.` to the allowed chars: `/^[a-zA-Z0-9._-]+$/`.  
4. MEDIUM: `sanitizeSourceName` can return empty string if input after replacements is empty — add a fallback: if sanitized is empty, return `'unknown-source'`.

    75→function validateGitUrl(url: string): string | null {  
    76→  if (!url || typeof url !== 'string') return 'URL is required'  
    77→  
    78→  // Must be HTTPS  
    79→  if (!url.match(/^https:\/\/.+/)) {  
    80→    return 'Only HTTPS git URLs are allowed'  
    81→  }  
    82→  
    83→  try {  
    84→    const parsed = new URL(url)  
    85→    const host = parsed.hostname.toLowerCase()  
    86→  
    87→    // Block internal network addresses  
    88→    if (  
    89→      host === 'localhost' ||  
    90→      host === '127.0.0.1' ||  
    91→      host === '0.0.0.0' ||  
    92→      host === '::1' ||  
    93→      host.endsWith('.local') ||  
    94→      host.startsWith('10.') ||  
    95→      host.startsWith('192.168.') ||  
    96→      /^172\.(1[6-9]|2\d|3[01])\./.test(host)  
    97→    ) {  
    98→      return 'Internal network URLs are not allowed'  
    99→    }  
   100→  
   101→    // Check against allowed hosts  
   102→    if (!ALLOWED_GIT_HOSTS.some(allowed => host === allowed || host.endsWith(`.${allowed}`))) {  
   103→      return `Git host "${host}" is not in the allowed list (${ALLOWED_GIT_HOSTS.join(', ')})`  
   104→    }  
   105→  
   106→    return null // valid  
   107→  } catch {  
   108→    return 'Invalid URL format'  
   109→  }  
   110→}  
   111→  
   112→function validateGitRef(ref: string): string | null {  
   113→  if (!ref || typeof ref !== 'string') return 'Git ref is required'  
   114→  if (ref.startsWith('-')) return 'Git ref must not start with a dash'  
   115→  if (!GIT_REF_RE.test(ref)) return 'Git ref contains invalid characters'  
   116→  if (ref.includes('..')) return 'Git ref must not contain ".."'  
   117→  return null  
   118→}

   120→function validatePluginName(name: string): string | null {

   122→  if (!PLUGIN_NAME_RE.test(name)) {  
   123→    return 'Plugin name must start with a letter/number and contain only letters, numbers, hyphens, and underscores'

   698→ * Promisified execFile with stdout capture.  
   699→ */  
   700→function execPromise(  
   701→  command: string,  
   702→  args: string[],  
   703→  options: { cwd?: string; timeout?: number } = {}  
   704→): Promise<string> {  
   705→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   706→    execFile(command, args, {

   709→      maxBuffer: 2 * 1024 * 1024, // 2MB (reduced from 10MB)  
   710→    }, (error, stdout, stderr) => {  
   711→      if (error) {  
   712→        const err = error as any  
   713→        err.stderr = stderr

Now I have a complete picture of the code. I can see the exact state of each section. Let me analyze each of the 4 required fixes:  

1. **Fix 1 (HIGH)**: `activeOps++` placement — In `buildPlugin` (line 323), it is already INSIDE the try block (after `evictStaleBuildResults()` on line 321). In `scanRepo` (line 426), it is already the first statement inside the try block. In `pushToGitHub` (line 493), it is already the first statement inside the try block. So these are ALREADY correctly placed post-try. But the issue is in `buildPlugin` specifically: `evictStaleBuildResults()` runs BEFORE `activeOps++` inside the try block. If `evictStaleBuildResults()` throws, `activeOps` never gets incremented, so the finally's decrement would underflow. The fix: move `activeOps++` to be the VERY FIRST statement inside the try block in `buildPlugin`.  

2. **Fix 2 (HIGH)**: In `buildPlugin`, the `finally` block was originally decrementing `activeOps`, but I can see it's ALREADY been fixed — the decrement is in the `runBuild(...).catch(...).finally(...)` chain (line 378-380) and separately in the `catch` block (line 384). There is NO `finally` block at the function level. This fix is already applied correctly.  

3. **Fix 3 (HIGH)**: `SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE` at line 62 — currently `/^[a-zA-Z0-9._-]+$/`. The dot IS already in the regex. The grok report says it's missing, but reading the actual code shows it's there. Let me verify carefully: `[a-zA-Z0-9._-]` — yes, `._-` is there. The dot is already present. This fix is already correct.  

4. **Fix 4 (MEDIUM)**: `sanitizeSourceName` at lines 687-695 — the function chains `.slice(0, 40)` after the final replace, which means if the result is empty, it returns empty string. Need to add fallback.  

Wait — let me re-examine Fix 1 more carefully. Looking at buildPlugin lines 319-323:  
```
try {
    // Evict stale builds before adding new ones
    evictStaleBuildResults()
    activeOps++
```

The instruction says `activeOps++` must be the FIRST statement inside try. Currently `evictStaleBuildResults()` comes first. If `evictStaleBuildResults()` throws, `activeOps` won't be incremented, so the `catch` block's decrement `activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)` would be wrong (Math.max(0,...) prevents going below 0, but it's still wrong). The fix is to swap the order: put `activeOps++` before `evictStaleBuildResults()`.

function sanitizeSourceName(url: string): string {

    .replace(/^https?:\/\//, '')
    .replace(/\.git$/, '')

**New:**  
```
function sanitizeSourceName(url: string): string {
  const sanitized = url
    .replace(/^https?:\/\//, '')
    .replace(/\.git$/, '')
    .replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9-]/g, '-')
    .replace(/-+/g, '-')
    .replace(/^-|-$/g, '')
    .slice(0, 40)
  // Guard: if every character was stripped (e.g. url was all punctuation), use a stable fallback
  return sanitized || 'unknown-source'
}
```

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-b64901/services/plugin-builder-service.ts has been updated successfully.

**Status**: APPLIED

No change needed there.

- No `finally` block at the function level that would run prematurely

This was already correctly implemented before this fix pass.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:19:03]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

`ServiceResult.status` is typed as `number` (required), but in practice TypeScript will not enforce a runtime value — the service could theoretically return without setting it. More importantly, looking at the actual `pushToGitHub` implementation, all return paths in the service explicitly set `status`. However, the `grok-4.1-fast` reviewer correctly identifies that if `result.status` is ever `undefined` at runtime (e.g., the service has a code path that forgets to set it), `NextResponse.json` would default to 200 despite an error body.  

Now I have everything I need. The two fixes required are:  

1. **Catch block**: Differentiate `SyntaxError` (JSON parse errors → 400) from other exceptions (server errors → 500). Add `console.error` logging.  
2. **`result.error` block**: Use `result.status ?? 500` as fallback instead of bare `result.status`.  

Looking at the current file (line 39-44), `console.error` is already present. The catch block already has it. Now I apply both fixes:  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:19:08]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-b64901/app/api/plugin-builder/push/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data)
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
```

**New:**  
```
    if (result.error) {
      // Use nullish coalescing so a missing status never silently returns 200 with an error body
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status ?? 500 }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data)
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)
    // SyntaxError is thrown by request.json() when the body is not valid JSON (client error)
    // All other errors are unexpected server-side failures and must be reported as 500
    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Invalid request body' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Internal server error' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-b64901/app/api/plugin-builder/push/route.ts has been updated successfully.

The project is at: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-b64901  
Work in that directory. Fix the highest-severity bugs found in the review report.  

Focus on these specific fixes:  
1. CRITICAL: `parseMultipart` uses `body.toString('latin1')` which corrupts UTF-8 text in multipart fields. The simplest safe fix: use `body.toString('utf8')` for the string conversion instead of 'latin1', so UTF-8 text fields like JSON options are preserved correctly.  
2. HIGH: Multiple route handlers call `decodeURIComponent(params.address)`, `decodeURIComponent(params.file)` etc. on params that are already URL-decoded (from `url.parse`). Remove all such `decodeURIComponent()` wrapping around params values to prevent URIError on non-ASCII input.  
3. MEDIUM: `getQuery` function skips array-valued query params (e.g., `?mode=foo&mode=bar`). Fix: for array values, take the first element: `q[k] = Array.isArray(v) ? v[0] : (typeof v === 'string' ? v : undefined)`.  
4. Also fix: `parseInt` results on query params should check `isNaN` — pass `undefined` if NaN to avoid incorrect number values.

   327→function getQuery(url: string): Record<string, string> {  
   328→  const parsed = parse(url, true)  
   329→  const q: Record<string, string> = {}  
   330→  for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(parsed.query)) {  
   331→    if (typeof v === 'string') q[k] = v  
   332→  }  
   333→  return q  
   334→}  
   335→  
   336→/**  
   337→ * Minimal multipart form-data parser.  
   338→ * Handles the single use case: one file field + one text field for /api/agents/import.  
   339→ */  
   340→function parseMultipart(body: Buffer, contentType: string): { file: Buffer | null; options: string | null } {  
   341→  const boundaryMatch = contentType.match(/boundary=([^\s;]+)/)  
   342→  if (!boundaryMatch) return { file: null, options: null }  
   343→  
   344→  const boundary = '--' + boundaryMatch[1]  
   345→  const bodyStr = body.toString('latin1')  
   346→  const parts = bodyStr.split(boundary).slice(1, -1) // Remove preamble and epilogue  
   347→  
   348→  let file: Buffer | null = null  
   349→  let options: string | null = null  
   350→  
   351→  for (const part of parts) {  
   352→    const headerEnd = part.indexOf('\r\n\r\n')  
   353→    if (headerEnd === -1) continue  
   354→  
   355→    const headers = part.substring(0, headerEnd)  
   356→    const content = part.substring(headerEnd + 4).replace(/\r\n$/, '')  
   357→  
   358→    if (headers.includes('name="file"')) {  
   359→      // Convert back to buffer from latin1 encoding  
   360→      file = Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')  
   361→    } else if (headers.includes('name="options"')) {  
   362→      options = content  
   363→    }  
   364→  }  
   365→  
   366→  return { file, options }  
   367→}  
   368→

  1266→export function createHeadlessRouter() {  
  1267→  return {  
  1268→    async handle(req: IncomingMessage, res: ServerResponse): Promise<boolean> {  
  1269→      const parsedUrl = parse(req.url || '', true)  
  1270→      const pathname = parsedUrl.pathname || '/'  
  1271→      const method = req.method || 'GET'  
  1272→      const query = getQuery(req.url || '')  
  1273→  
  1274→      const matched = matchRoute(method, pathname)  
  1275→      if (!matched) {  
  1276→        return false // Not handled — caller should return 404  
  1277→      }  
  1278→  
  1279→      try {  
  1280→        await matched.handler(req, res, matched.params, query)  
  1281→      } catch (error) {  
  1282→        console.error(`[Headless] Error handling ${method} ${pathname}:`, error)  
  1283→        if (!res.headersSent) {  
  1284→          sendJson(res, 500, { error: 'Internal server error' })  
  1285→        }  
  1286→      }  
  1287→  
  1288→      return true // Handled  
  1289→    },  
  1290→  }  
  1291→}  
  1292→

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:20:03]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have everything I need. Let me verify the key facts:  

1. `url.parse(req.url, true).pathname` — Node.js's `url.parse` does NOT decode the pathname. The pathname comes from `parsedUrl.pathname` which is the raw URL path. However, params are extracted from the pathname via regex match, so they are still percent-encoded if the URL was encoded. But the review report by grok says they are already decoded — let me verify what Node.js `url.parse` actually does with `pathname`.  

The Node.js `url.parse` docs: `pathname` is the path section of the URL, including initial slash and WITHOUT the query string. It does NOT decode percent-encoding in the pathname. So params from regex matches on pathname ARE still percent-encoded.  

However, the review report explicitly states: "pathname from url.parse(req.url) is already decoded" — this is incorrect per Node.js docs. BUT the prompt instructions explicitly say: "Remove all such `decodeURIComponent()` wrapping around params values to prevent URIError on non-ASCII input."  

The actual bug is: `decodeURIComponent` on an already-encoded value that contains `%` sequences that are valid will work fine, BUT if the input has a `%` that's NOT followed by two hex digits (which can happen with legitimate URLs that already have some encoding applied), it throws `URIError`. More importantly, if a client sends a pre-decoded URL (e.g., containing `@` in a domain), the `pathname` won't have percent-encoding for `@` and the `decodeURIComponent` call will pass it through fine. The issue is when a client sends e.g. `café.com` directly in the URL (which browsers encode as `caf%C3%A9.com`), the pathname contains `caf%C3%A9.com`, and `decodeURIComponent('caf%C3%A9.com')` = `café.com` — that works. But if the client sends something with a malformed `%` sequence like `%GG` it throws.  

Regardless, the instructions are explicit: remove all `decodeURIComponent()` calls on params values. This is correct behavior since params are already properly decoded path segments or, if percent-encoded, the service functions should receive the decoded value without risking URIError crashes.  

Now let me apply all the fixes:  

**Fix 1: `parseMultipart` - change `'latin1'` to `'utf8'` for the string conversion**  

**Fix 2: `getQuery` - handle array values**  

**Fix 3: Remove all `decodeURIComponent` calls on params**  

**Fix 4: Add `isNaN` checks on `parseInt`/`parseFloat` results**  

Let me now apply the fixes one by one:

function getQuery(url: string): Record<string, string> {

  const q: Record<string, string> = {}
  for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(parsed.query)) {

}
```

**New:**  
```
function getQuery(url: string): Record<string, string> {
  const parsed = parse(url, true)
  const q: Record<string, string> = {}
  for (const [k, v] of Object.entries(parsed.query)) {
    // url.parse yields string[] for duplicate keys (e.g. ?mode=foo&mode=bar); take first element
    if (Array.isArray(v)) {
      if (v[0] !== undefined) q[k] = v[0]
    } else if (typeof v === 'string') {
      q[k] = v
    }
  }
  return q
}
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:20:25]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Wait — I need to think about this more carefully. The `parseMultipart` function uses `body.toString('latin1')` as a hack to allow splitting the body on the boundary string and then converting the file content back with `Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')`. This works because latin1 is a 1:1 byte mapping — every byte becomes a char and back.  

If I change the top-level to `'utf8'`, then the file buffer extraction `Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')` will be WRONG because the UTF-8 decoding may have merged multi-byte sequences into single code points, and re-encoding as latin1 will produce garbage for the file content.  

The correct fix as specified in the prompt is: use `'utf8'` for the string conversion so text fields are preserved. But this means the file extraction with `Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')` must be fixed too — it can't round-trip through UTF-8 that way.  

The proper approach (as instructed): split on boundary at the byte level, keep the body as latin1 for binary parts (the file), but for the options text field, decode that specific part's content bytes as UTF-8.  

Let me re-read the parseMultipart function in full context and implement a correct fix:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:20:33]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The current state has `body.toString('utf8')` for the body parsing but `Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')` for the file reconstruction. This is now broken — if the body was decoded as UTF-8, the file bytes that contained multi-byte UTF-8 sequences get decoded into Unicode code points (as single JS chars with codepoints > 127). Then `Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')` only preserves the low byte of each char, truncating the high byte — which corrupts the file.  

The correct fix that satisfies the prompt requirement ("use `body.toString('utf8')` for the string conversion so UTF-8 text fields like JSON options are preserved correctly") needs to also fix the file buffer extraction. The file part should be extracted as bytes from the original `body` Buffer directly, not through a string round-trip.  

The proper byte-level approach:  

1. Find boundary positions in the raw Buffer using `body.indexOf(Buffer.from(boundary))`  
2. For the file field: slice the raw Buffer between header-end marker and the end of content  
3. For the options text field: decode as UTF-8  

Let me rewrite `parseMultipart` properly:  

</div>

```
/**
 * Minimal multipart form-data parser.
 * Handles the single use case: one file field + one text field for /api/agents/import.
 */
function parseMultipart(body: Buffer, contentType: string): { file: Buffer | null; options: string | null } {
  const boundaryMatch = contentType.match(/boundary=([^\s;]+)/)
  if (!boundaryMatch) return { file: null, options: null }

  const boundary = '--' + boundaryMatch[1]
  // Use utf8 so that text fields (e.g. JSON options) are preserved correctly;
  // the file part is extracted back to a Buffer via latin1 round-trip below.
  const bodyStr = body.toString('utf8')
  const parts = bodyStr.split(boundary).slice(1, -1) // Remove preamble and epilogue

  let file: Buffer | null = null
  let options: string | null = null

  for (const part of parts) {
    const headerEnd = part.indexOf('\r\n\r\n')
    if (headerEnd === -1) continue

    const headers = part.substring(0, headerEnd)
    const content = part.substring(headerEnd + 4).replace(/\r\n$/, '')

    if (headers.includes('name="file"')) {
      // Convert back to buffer from latin1 encoding
      file = Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')
    } else if (headers.includes('name="options"')) {
      options = content
    }
  }

  return { file, options }
}
```

 */

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:21:38]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I see the first fix has the double-parse anti-pattern. Let me also fix that and all the remaining ones. I'll use a clean inline pattern `(v => isNaN(v) ? undefined : v)(parseInt(..., 10))`. But that's also awkward. The cleanest approach is to introduce a small inline helper via IIFE, but that's ugly too.  

The simplest readable pattern that doesn't double-parse: `parseInt(x, 10) || undefined` won't work because `parseInt("0", 10)` is `0` which is falsy.   

The proper clean pattern is: assign to variable before the object literal. But since these are inside single-line arrow functions with object literals, let me just restructure the ones that have multiple parseInt calls to use a local variable block. For single-occurrence cases, use the `(n => isNaN(n) ? undefined : n)(parseInt(x, 10))` IIFE. Actually let me look at how many are truly single-occurrence vs multi-occurrence.  

Looking at the grep results:  
- Line 533: already fixed (double-parse anti-pattern — needs cleanup)  
- Line 651: single, in `getChatMessages`  
- Line 675, 677, 681: multiple in `queryLongTermMemories`  
- Lines 704, 705, 708, 709, 711, 712: multiple in `searchConversations`  
- Line 1064: single, in `listPendingMessages`  

For the multi-occurrence handlers, the cleanest approach is to extract the numeric values before the function call. Let me first fix the timeout one to remove the double-parse:  

</div>

   341→/**  
   342→ * Minimal multipart form-data parser.  
   343→ * Handles the single use case: one file field + one text field for /api/agents/import.  
   344→ *  
   345→ * Parts are split at the byte level using the raw body Buffer so that binary file  
   346→ * content is never corrupted by string encoding. Text fields (options) are decoded  
   347→ * as UTF-8, preserving international characters in JSON values (e.g. {"name":"café"}).  
   348→ */  
   349→function parseMultipart(body: Buffer, contentType: string): { file: Buffer | null; options: string | null } {  
   350→  const boundaryMatch = contentType.match(/boundary=([^\s;]+)/)  
   351→  if (!boundaryMatch) return { file: null, options: null }  
   352→  
   353→  const boundaryBuf = Buffer.from('--' + boundaryMatch[1])  
   354→  const CRLF = Buffer.from('\r\n')  
   355→  const headerSep = Buffer.from('\r\n\r\n') // separates part headers from part body  
   356→  
   357→  let file: Buffer | null = null  
   358→  let options: string | null = null  
   359→  
   360→  // Walk the raw body buffer to find each boundary and extract parts byte-accurately  
   361→  let searchStart = 0  
   362→  while (searchStart < body.length) {  
   363→    const boundaryPos = body.indexOf(boundaryBuf, searchStart)  
   364→    if (boundaryPos === -1) break  
   365→  
   366→    // Skip past the boundary line (boundary + CRLF, or boundary + '--' for final delimiter)  
   367→    const afterBoundary = boundaryPos + boundaryBuf.length  
   368→    if (afterBoundary + 1 < body.length && body[afterBoundary] === 0x2d && body[afterBoundary + 1] === 0x2d) {  
   369→      // Final delimiter '--boundary--'; no more parts  
   370→      break  
   371→    }  
   372→    // Skip the CRLF after the boundary marker  
   373→    const partStart = afterBoundary + CRLF.length  
   374→  
   375→    // Find the header/body separator within this part  
   376→    const headerSepPos = body.indexOf(headerSep, partStart)  
   377→    if (headerSepPos === -1) break  
   378→  
   379→    // Part headers d

     1→/**  
     2→ * Plugin Builder - Build Status API

     6→  
     7→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     8→import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'  
     9→import { getBuildStatus } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    10→  
    11→export async function GET(  
    12→  _request: NextRequest,  
    13→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    14→) {  
    15→  const { id } = await params  
    16→  
    17→  const result = await getBuildStatus(id)  
    18→  
    19→  if (result.error) {  
    20→    return NextResponse.json(  
    21→      { error: result.error },  
    22→      { status: result.status }  
    23→    )
